Motif Inferensi, Eksplanasi dan P ---  --- SUMBER 2: Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- General description of the scales --- The DASS is a set of three self-report scales designed to measure the negative emotional states of depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS was constructed not merely as another set of scales to measure conventionally defined emotional states, but to further the process of defining, understanding, and measuring the ubiquitous and clinically significant emotional states usually described as depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS should thus meet the requirements of both researchers and scientist-professional clinicians. --- Each of the three DASS scales contains 14 items, divided into subscales of 2-5 items with similar content.  The Depression scale assesses dysphoria, hopelessness, devaluation of life, self-deprecation, lack of interest/involvement, anhedonia, and inertia.  The Anxiety scale assesses autonomic arousal, skeletal muscle effects, situational anxiety, and subjective experience of anxious affect.  The Stress scale is sensitive to levels of chronic non-specific arousal.  It assesses difficulty relaxing, nervous arousal, and being easily upset/agitated, irritable/over-reactive and impatient.  Subjects are asked to use 4-point severity/frequency scales to rate the extent to which they have experienced each state --- over the past week --- .  Scores for Depression, Anxiety and Stress are calculated by summing the scores for the relevant items. --- In addition to the basic 42-item questionnaire, a short version, the DASS21, is available with 7 items per scale.  Note also that an earlier version of the DASS scales was referred to as the Self-Analysis Questionnaire (SAQ). --- As the scales of the DASS have been shown to have high internal consistency and to yield meaningful discriminations in a variety of settings, the scales should meet the needs of both researchers and clinicians who wish to measure current state or change in state over time (e.g., in the course of treatment) on the three dimensions of depression, anxiety and stress. --- Characteristics of high scorers on each DASS scale --- Depression scale --- self-disparaging --- dispirited, gloomy, blue --- convinced that life has no meaning or value --- pessimistic about the future --- unable to experience enjoyment or satisfaction --- unable to become interested or involved --- slow, lacking in initiative --- Anxiety scale --- apprehensive, panicky --- trembly, shaky --- aware of dryness of the mouth, breathing difficulties, pounding of the heart, sweatiness of the palms --- worried about performance and possible loss of control --- Stress scale --- over-aroused, tense --- unable to relax --- touchy, easily upset --- irritable --- easily startled --- nervy, jumpy, fidgety --- intolerant of interruption or delay --- The DASS in research --- The DASS may be administered either in groups or individually for research purposes.  The capacity to discriminate between the three related states of depression, anxiety and stress should be useful to researchers concerned with the nature, aetiology and mechanisms of emotional disturbance. --- As the essential development of the DASS was carried out with non-clinical samples, it is suitable for screening normal adolescents and adults.  Given the necessary language proficiency, there seems no compelling case against use of the scales for comparative purposes with children as young as 12 years.  It must be borne in mind, however, that the lower age limit of the development samples was 17 years. --- Clinical use of the DASS --- The principal value of the DASS in a clinical setting is to clarify the locus of emotional disturbance, as part of the broader task of clinical assessment.  The essential function of the DASS is to assess the severity of the --- core --- symptoms of depression, anxiety and stress.  It must be recognised that clinically depressed, anxious or stressed persons may well manifest additional symptoms that tend to be common to two or all three of the conditions, such as sleep, appetite, and sexual disturbances.  These disturbances will be elicited by clinical examination, or by the use of general symptom check lists as required. --- The DASS may be administered and scored by non-psychologists, but decisions based on particular score profiles should be made only by experienced clinicians who have carried out an appropriate clinical examination.  It should be noted also that none of the DASS items refers to suicidal tendencies because items relating to such tendencies were found not to load on any scale.  The experienced clinician will recognise the need to determine the risk of suicide in seriously disturbed persons. --- The DASS and diagnosis --- The DASS is based on a --- dimensional --- rather than a --- categorical --- conception of psychological disorder.  The assumption on which the DASS development was based (and which was confirmed by the research data) is that the differences between the depression, the anxiety, and the stress experienced by normal subjects and the clinically disturbed, are essentially differences of degree. 22-Apr-2026-10:26:29|IDED4857|CHATGPT[8]="Kalau aku tangkap, meski kerjaan selesai kamu sempat lega, tapi itu sifatnya sementara—karena “aftertaste”-nya tetap ada: tugas berikutnya sudah terasa, dan ditambah lagi kamu tidak yakin apakah yang dikerjakan benar. Jadi tegangnya bukan cuma dari tugas saat itu, tapi dari kekhawatiran yang menggantung bahkan setelah selesai. Ini nyambung dengan skor stress tinggi dan anxiety yang cukup kuat: tubuh tegang terus, lalu muncul keraguan “gimana kalau salah” yang bikin kamu sulit bener-bener turun. Rasa kehilangan inisiatif dan sulit merasakan hal positif juga bisa muncul ketika otak terlalu lama berada di mode waspada seperti ini. ---  --- Aku mau tanya satu pertanyaan penting supaya kita bisa mengarah ke pemecahan yang lebih spesifik: biasanya kamu mendapat kepastian benar/salah itu dari siapa (guru/atasan/teman/penilaian sistem), dan kapan hasilnya biasanya keluar?"

22-Apr-2026-10:26:52|IDED4857|CHATGPT[9]="Wah, itu jelas bikin makin berat. Kalau penilaian benar/salah ada di tangan atasan dan jadwal/ketentuannya tidak jelas (suka-suka), maka otak kamu sulit membangun “landmark”: tidak ada patokan waktu dan kepastian, jadi kamu tetap berjaga-jaga. Pola ini bisa menyalakan kecemasan “kalau aku salah gimana” dan stress “harus cepat selesai biar selesai”, tapi karena kepastian tidak datang, tegangnya tidak benar-benar turun—akhirnya kerjaan terasa seperti ancaman yang terus bisa muncul kapan saja. Ini juga menjelaskan mengapa kamu bangun tidak segar: sistem stres kemungkinan tetap aktif saat malam. ---  --- Satu pertanyaan tindak lanjut: saat atasan memberikan tugas atau instruksi, apakah pernah ada contoh standar/rujukan (misalnya format yang benar, contoh tugas yang bagus, atau checklist), atau semuanya lebih berupa instruksi umum tanpa pedoman?"

Dalam situasi seperti itu, kecemasan takut salah itu jadi sangat masuk akal, dan kerjaan numpuk juga jadi terasa “tak berujung” karena kamu nggak bisa memverifikasi diri dengan cepat. Akibatnya, meski kamu langsung mengerjakan, otak tetap tidak dapat sinyal “aman” sehingga stress kamu tetap tinggi, yang kemudian ikut memengaruhi emosi (jadi sedih/kehilangan minat/merasa tidak berharga) dan tubuh (susah rileks, gampang tersinggung, gejala tegang). ---  --- Sekarang aku perlu satu pertanyaan untuk mengarahkan langkah yang paling realistis: dari semua tugas yang kamu kerjakan, tugas seperti apa yang paling bikin kamu merasa takut salah/kurang mampu (misalnya deadline, hasil akhir yang dinilai, presentasi, ketelitian, atau yang sifatnya kreatif tanpa format)?"

Ketika semua tugas terasa berisiko salah, otak kamu akan menganggap setiap pekerjaan sebagai ancaman, sehingga mode cemas dan tegang terus menyala, lalu memanjang ke depresi sedang (misalnya sulit merasakan hal positif dan merasa tidak berharga) dan stress tinggi (sulit rileks, mudah bereaksi berlebihan). ---  --- Satu pertanyaan terakhir (biar aku bisa bantu bikin cara yang paling cocok): kamu pernah coba minta kejelasan ke atasan (misalnya “boleh ada contoh/format yang benar?” atau “tolong konfirmasi sebelum saya lanjut”), atau kamu biasanya menahan diri dulu karena takut dianggap merepotkan?"

Dampaknya terlihat dari skor kamu: stress tinggi (sulit rileks, mudah terganggu/terpicu, mudah tersinggung), anxiety yang cukup tinggi (khawatir panik/biang-bingung, gejala tegang), dan depresi sedang (kehilangan inisiatif, sulit merasakan hal positif, merasa tidak berharga). Selain itu, tidur yang tidak segar bisa memperkuat semuanya karena otak makin sensitif terhadap ancaman. ---  --- Aku mau tanya satu hal yang penting banget untuk keselamatan emosionalmu: selama beberapa waktu belakangan ini, pernah muncul pikiran menyakiti diri atau merasa ingin menghilang, atau itu tidak pernah muncul sama sekali?"

22-Apr-2026-10:28:45|IDED4857|RINGKASAN="Identitas Siswa --- Fauzul Arifin, siswa kelas 12A ---  --- Jenis Temuan --- 1) Tingkat stres tinggi: sulit bersantai, tegang, mudah tersinggung/overreaktif, gelisah dan sulit menoleransi penundaan. --- 2) Tingkat kecemasan sedang-cukup tinggi: khawatir panik/akan membuat bodoh, takut salah/kurang mampu, disertai gejala fisiologis seperti gemetar dan rasa tidak enak di tubuh. --- 3) Tingkat depresi sedang: sulit merasakan perasaan positif, kehilangan minat, merasa tidak berharga, dan kesulitan memunculkan inisiatif. --- Pola pemicu utama: kerjaan menumpuk, kebutuhan “harus cepat selesai agar bisa pulih”, instruksi umum tanpa pedoman, serta kepastian penilaian yang tidak jelas karena ditentukan suka-suka oleh atasan; diperkuat oleh kualitas tidur yang buruk (susah tidur awal, bangun telat, tidak segar). ---  --- Skor Risiko --- Depresi: 11 (sedang sampai mengarah ke mengganggu) --- Kecemasan/Anxiety: 9 (cukup nyata, sedang) --- Stress: 21 (tertinggi dan paling menonjol) ---  --- Rekomendasi Tindakan --- 1) Prioritaskan pemulihan inti: buat target kecil untuk tidur (mis. jadwal tidur paling awal 15–30 menit lebih maju dari biasanya) dan buat rutinitas penurunan tegang 20 menit sebelum tidur (mis. berhenti kerja 20 menit, mandi/relaks napas, atur lampu redup). --- 2) Kurangi ketidakpastian saat kerja: sebelum mengerjakan, tulis ulang instruksi atasan dalam 3 poin, lalu minta konfirmasi singkat hanya untuk hal paling krusial (boleh lewat pesan singkat/“konfirmasi format/jawaban yang diharapkan” sekali per paket tugas, bukan tiap tugas). --- 3) Gunakan “jeda selesai” yang realistis: setelah menyelesaikan satu bagian, lakukan cek cepat sesuai aturan yang kamu buat sendiri (mis. checklist 5 item) dan berhenti dulu 3–5 menit untuk menurunkan tegang sebelum lanjut bagian berikutnya. --- 4) Untuk menurunkan tegang yang berulang: latih teknik relaksasi sederhana (napas perlahan 4-6 siklus, lalu rilekskan bahu dan rahang) saat mulai merasa gelisah atau sebelum mulai tugas. --- 5) Karena stress dan depresi sedang serta tidur terganggu, pertimbangkan dukungan lanjutan dari konselor/psikolog sekolah atau profesional agar ada rencana pemulihan yang lebih terstruktur."

Intelegensi - 85  --- x  ---   --- 4. Belajar - 93  --- B. Gejala Emosi - 107  --- 1. Emosi - 107  --- 2. Teori-Teori Emosi  - 109  --- C. Gejala Konasi - 121  --- 1. Motif Inferensi, Eksplanasi dan P ---  --- SUMBER 2: Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- General description of the scales --- The DASS is a set of three self-report scales designed to measure the negative emotional states of depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS was constructed not merely as another set of scales to measure conventionally defined emotional states, but to further the process of defining, understanding, and measuring the ubiquitous and clinically significant emotional states usually described as depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS should thus meet the requirements of both researchers and scientist-professional clinicians. --- Each of the three DASS scales contains 14 items, divided into subscales of 2-5 items with similar content.  The Depression scale assesses dysphoria, hopelessness, devaluation of life, self-deprecation, lack of interest/involvement, anhedonia, and inertia.  The Anxiety scale assesses autonomic arousal, skeletal muscle effects, situational anxiety, and subjective experience of anxious affect.  The Stress scale is sensitive to levels of chronic non-specific arousal.  It assesses difficulty relaxing, nervous arousal, and being easily upset/agitated, irritable/over-reactive and impatient.  Subjects are asked to use 4-point severity/frequency scales to rate the extent to which they have experienced each state --- over the past week --- .  Scores for Depression, Anxiety and Stress are calculated by summing the scores for the relevant items. --- In addition to the basic 42-item questionnaire, a short version, the DASS21, is available with 7 items per scale.  Note also that an earlier version of the DASS scales was referred to as the Self-Analysis Questionnaire (SAQ). --- As the scales of the DASS have been shown to have high internal consistency and to yield meaningful discriminations in a variety of settings, the scales should meet the needs of both researchers and clinicians who wish to measure current state or change in state over time (e.g., in the course of treatment) on the three dimensions of depression, anxiety and stress. --- Characteristics of high scorers on each DASS scale --- Depression scale --- self-disparaging --- dispirited, gloomy, blue --- convinced that life has no meaning or value --- pessimistic about the future --- unable to experience enjoyment or satisfaction --- unable to become interested or involved --- slow, lacking in initiative --- Anxiety scale --- apprehensive, panicky --- trembly, shaky --- aware of dryness of the mouth, breathing difficulties, pounding of the heart, sweatiness of the palms --- worried about performance and possible loss of control --- Stress scale --- over-aroused, tense --- unable to relax --- touchy, easily upset --- irritable --- easily startled --- nervy, jumpy, fidgety --- intolerant of interruption or delay --- The DASS in research --- The DASS may be administered either in groups or individually for research purposes.  The capacity to discriminate between the three related states of depression, anxiety and stress should be useful to researchers concerned with the nature, aetiology and mechanisms of emotional disturbance. --- As the essential development of the DASS was carried out with non-clinical samples, it is suitable for screening normal adolescents and adults.  Given the necessary language proficiency, there seems no compelling case against use of the scales for comparative purposes with children as young as 12 years.  It must be borne in mind, however, that the lower age limit of the development samples was 17 years. --- Clinical use of the DASS --- The principal value of the DASS in a clinical setting is to clarify the locus of emotional disturbance, as part of the broader task of clinical assessment.  The essential function of the DASS is to assess the severity of the --- core --- symptoms of depression, anxiety and stress.  It must be recognised that clinically depressed, anxious or stressed persons may well manifest additional symptoms that tend to be common to two or all three of the conditions, such as sleep, appetite, and sexual disturbances.  These disturbances will be elicited by clinical examination, or by the use of general symptom check lists as required. --- The DASS may be administered and scored by non-psychologists, but decisions based on particular score profiles should be made only by experienced clinicians who have carried out an appropriate clinical examination.  It should be noted also that none of the DASS items refers to suicidal tendencies because items relating to such tendencies were found not to load on any scale.  The experienced clinician will recognise the need to determine the risk of suicide in seriously disturbed persons. --- The DASS and diagnosis --- The DASS is based on a --- dimensional --- rather than a --- categorical --- conception of psychological disorder.  The assumption on which the DASS development was based (and which was confirmed by the research data) is that the differences between the depression, the anxiety, and the stress experienced by normal subjects and the clinically disturbed, are essentially differences of degree. Motif Inferensi, Eksplanasi dan P ---  --- SUMBER 2: Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- General description of the scales --- The DASS is a set of three self-report scales designed to measure the negative emotional states of depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS was constructed not merely as another set of scales to measure conventionally defined emotional states, but to further the process of defining, understanding, and measuring the ubiquitous and clinically significant emotional states usually described as depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS should thus meet the requirements of both researchers and scientist-professional clinicians. --- Each of the three DASS scales contains 14 items, divided into subscales of 2-5 items with similar content.  The Depression scale assesses dysphoria, hopelessness, devaluation of life, self-deprecation, lack of interest/involvement, anhedonia, and inertia.  The Anxiety scale assesses autonomic arousal, skeletal muscle effects, situational anxiety, and subjective experience of anxious affect.  The Stress scale is sensitive to levels of chronic non-specific arousal.  It assesses difficulty relaxing, nervous arousal, and being easily upset/agitated, irritable/over-reactive and impatient.  Subjects are asked to use 4-point severity/frequency scales to rate the extent to which they have experienced each state --- over the past week --- .  Scores for Depression, Anxiety and Stress are calculated by summing the scores for the relevant items. --- In addition to the basic 42-item questionnaire, a short version, the DASS21, is available with 7 items per scale.  Note also that an earlier version of the DASS scales was referred to as the Self-Analysis Questionnaire (SAQ). --- As the scales of the DASS have been shown to have high internal consistency and to yield meaningful discriminations in a variety of settings, the scales should meet the needs of both researchers and clinicians who wish to measure current state or change in state over time (e.g., in the course of treatment) on the three dimensions of depression, anxiety and stress. --- Characteristics of high scorers on each DASS scale --- Depression scale --- self-disparaging --- dispirited, gloomy, blue --- convinced that life has no meaning or value --- pessimistic about the future --- unable to experience enjoyment or satisfaction --- unable to become interested or involved --- slow, lacking in initiative --- Anxiety scale --- apprehensive, panicky --- trembly, shaky --- aware of dryness of the mouth, breathing difficulties, pounding of the heart, sweatiness of the palms --- worried about performance and possible loss of control --- Stress scale --- over-aroused, tense --- unable to relax --- touchy, easily upset --- irritable --- easily startled --- nervy, jumpy, fidgety --- intolerant of interruption or delay --- The DASS in research --- The DASS may be administered either in groups or individually for research purposes.  The capacity to discriminate between the three related states of depression, anxiety and stress should be useful to researchers concerned with the nature, aetiology and mechanisms of emotional disturbance. --- As the essential development of the DASS was carried out with non-clinical samples, it is suitable for screening normal adolescents and adults.  Given the necessary language proficiency, there seems no compelling case against use of the scales for comparative purposes with children as young as 12 years.  It must be borne in mind, however, that the lower age limit of the development samples was 17 years. --- Clinical use of the DASS --- The principal value of the DASS in a clinical setting is to clarify the locus of emotional disturbance, as part of the broader task of clinical assessment.  The essential function of the DASS is to assess the severity of the --- core --- symptoms of depression, anxiety and stress.  It must be recognised that clinically depressed, anxious or stressed persons may well manifest additional symptoms that tend to be common to two or all three of the conditions, such as sleep, appetite, and sexual disturbances.  These disturbances will be elicited by clinical examination, or by the use of general symptom check lists as required. --- The DASS may be administered and scored by non-psychologists, but decisions based on particular score profiles should be made only by experienced clinicians who have carried out an appropriate clinical examination.  It should be noted also that none of the DASS items refers to suicidal tendencies because items relating to such tendencies were found not to load on any scale.  The experienced clinician will recognise the need to determine the risk of suicide in seriously disturbed persons. --- The DASS and diagnosis --- The DASS is based on a --- dimensional --- rather than a --- categorical --- conception of psychological disorder.  The assumption on which the DASS development was based (and which was confirmed by the research data) is that the differences between the depression, the anxiety, and the stress experienced by normal subjects and the clinically disturbed, are essentially differences of degree. Motif Inferensi, Eksplanasi dan P ---  --- SUMBER 2: Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- General description of the scales --- The DASS is a set of three self-report scales designed to measure the negative emotional states of depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS was constructed not merely as another set of scales to measure conventionally defined emotional states, but to further the process of defining, understanding, and measuring the ubiquitous and clinically significant emotional states usually described as depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS should thus meet the requirements of both researchers and scientist-professional clinicians. --- Each of the three DASS scales contains 14 items, divided into subscales of 2-5 items with similar content.  The Depression scale assesses dysphoria, hopelessness, devaluation of life, self-deprecation, lack of interest/involvement, anhedonia, and inertia.  The Anxiety scale assesses autonomic arousal, skeletal muscle effects, situational anxiety, and subjective experience of anxious affect.  The Stress scale is sensitive to levels of chronic non-specific arousal.  It assesses difficulty relaxing, nervous arousal, and being easily upset/agitated, irritable/over-reactive and impatient.  Subjects are asked to use 4-point severity/frequency scales to rate the extent to which they have experienced each state --- over the past week --- .  Scores for Depression, Anxiety and Stress are calculated by summing the scores for the relevant items. --- In addition to the basic 42-item questionnaire, a short version, the DASS21, is available with 7 items per scale.  Note also that an earlier version of the DASS scales was referred to as the Self-Analysis Questionnaire (SAQ). --- As the scales of the DASS have been shown to have high internal consistency and to yield meaningful discriminations in a variety of settings, the scales should meet the needs of both researchers and clinicians who wish to measure current state or change in state over time (e.g., in the course of treatment) on the three dimensions of depression, anxiety and stress. --- Characteristics of high scorers on each DASS scale --- Depression scale --- self-disparaging --- dispirited, gloomy, blue --- convinced that life has no meaning or value --- pessimistic about the future --- unable to experience enjoyment or satisfaction --- unable to become interested or involved --- slow, lacking in initiative --- Anxiety scale --- apprehensive, panicky --- trembly, shaky --- aware of dryness of the mouth, breathing difficulties, pounding of the heart, sweatiness of the palms --- worried about performance and possible loss of control --- Stress scale --- over-aroused, tense --- unable to relax --- touchy, easily upset --- irritable --- easily startled --- nervy, jumpy, fidgety --- intolerant of interruption or delay --- The DASS in research --- The DASS may be administered either in groups or individually for research purposes.  The capacity to discriminate between the three related states of depression, anxiety and stress should be useful to researchers concerned with the nature, aetiology and mechanisms of emotional disturbance. --- As the essential development of the DASS was carried out with non-clinical samples, it is suitable for screening normal adolescents and adults.  Given the necessary language proficiency, there seems no compelling case against use of the scales for comparative purposes with children as young as 12 years.  It must be borne in mind, however, that the lower age limit of the development samples was 17 years. --- Clinical use of the DASS --- The principal value of the DASS in a clinical setting is to clarify the locus of emotional disturbance, as part of the broader task of clinical assessment.  The essential function of the DASS is to assess the severity of the --- core --- symptoms of depression, anxiety and stress.  It must be recognised that clinically depressed, anxious or stressed persons may well manifest additional symptoms that tend to be common to two or all three of the conditions, such as sleep, appetite, and sexual disturbances.  These disturbances will be elicited by clinical examination, or by the use of general symptom check lists as required. --- The DASS may be administered and scored by non-psychologists, but decisions based on particular score profiles should be made only by experienced clinicians who have carried out an appropriate clinical examination.  It should be noted also that none of the DASS items refers to suicidal tendencies because items relating to such tendencies were found not to load on any scale.  The experienced clinician will recognise the need to determine the risk of suicide in seriously disturbed persons. --- The DASS and diagnosis --- The DASS is based on a --- dimensional --- rather than a --- categorical --- conception of psychological disorder.  The assumption on which the DASS development was based (and which was confirmed by the research data) is that the differences between the depression, the anxiety, and the stress experienced by normal subjects and the clinically disturbed, are essentially differences of degree. Motif Inferensi, Eksplanasi dan P ---  --- SUMBER 2: Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- General description of the scales --- The DASS is a set of three self-report scales designed to measure the negative emotional states of depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS was constructed not merely as another set of scales to measure conventionally defined emotional states, but to further the process of defining, understanding, and measuring the ubiquitous and clinically significant emotional states usually described as depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS should thus meet the requirements of both researchers and scientist-professional clinicians. --- Each of the three DASS scales contains 14 items, divided into subscales of 2-5 items with similar content.  The Depression scale assesses dysphoria, hopelessness, devaluation of life, self-deprecation, lack of interest/involvement, anhedonia, and inertia.  The Anxiety scale assesses autonomic arousal, skeletal muscle effects, situational anxiety, and subjective experience of anxious affect.  The Stress scale is sensitive to levels of chronic non-specific arousal.  It assesses difficulty relaxing, nervous arousal, and being easily upset/agitated, irritable/over-reactive and impatient.  Subjects are asked to use 4-point severity/frequency scales to rate the extent to which they have experienced each state --- over the past week --- .  Scores for Depression, Anxiety and Stress are calculated by summing the scores for the relevant items. --- In addition to the basic 42-item questionnaire, a short version, the DASS21, is available with 7 items per scale.  Note also that an earlier version of the DASS scales was referred to as the Self-Analysis Questionnaire (SAQ). --- As the scales of the DASS have been shown to have high internal consistency and to yield meaningful discriminations in a variety of settings, the scales should meet the needs of both researchers and clinicians who wish to measure current state or change in state over time (e.g., in the course of treatment) on the three dimensions of depression, anxiety and stress. --- Characteristics of high scorers on each DASS scale --- Depression scale --- self-disparaging --- dispirited, gloomy, blue --- convinced that life has no meaning or value --- pessimistic about the future --- unable to experience enjoyment or satisfaction --- unable to become interested or involved --- slow, lacking in initiative --- Anxiety scale --- apprehensive, panicky --- trembly, shaky --- aware of dryness of the mouth, breathing difficulties, pounding of the heart, sweatiness of the palms --- worried about performance and possible loss of control --- Stress scale --- over-aroused, tense --- unable to relax --- touchy, easily upset --- irritable --- easily startled --- nervy, jumpy, fidgety --- intolerant of interruption or delay --- The DASS in research --- The DASS may be administered either in groups or individually for research purposes.  The capacity to discriminate between the three related states of depression, anxiety and stress should be useful to researchers concerned with the nature, aetiology and mechanisms of emotional disturbance. --- As the essential development of the DASS was carried out with non-clinical samples, it is suitable for screening normal adolescents and adults.  Given the necessary language proficiency, there seems no compelling case against use of the scales for comparative purposes with children as young as 12 years.  It must be borne in mind, however, that the lower age limit of the development samples was 17 years. --- Clinical use of the DASS --- The principal value of the DASS in a clinical setting is to clarify the locus of emotional disturbance, as part of the broader task of clinical assessment.  The essential function of the DASS is to assess the severity of the --- core --- symptoms of depression, anxiety and stress.  It must be recognised that clinically depressed, anxious or stressed persons may well manifest additional symptoms that tend to be common to two or all three of the conditions, such as sleep, appetite, and sexual disturbances.  These disturbances will be elicited by clinical examination, or by the use of general symptom check lists as required. --- The DASS may be administered and scored by non-psychologists, but decisions based on particular score profiles should be made only by experienced clinicians who have carried out an appropriate clinical examination.  It should be noted also that none of the DASS items refers to suicidal tendencies because items relating to such tendencies were found not to load on any scale.  The experienced clinician will recognise the need to determine the risk of suicide in seriously disturbed persons. --- The DASS and diagnosis --- The DASS is based on a --- dimensional --- rather than a --- categorical --- conception of psychological disorder.  The assumption on which the DASS development was based (and which was confirmed by the research data) is that the differences between the depression, the anxiety, and the stress experienced by normal subjects and the clinically disturbed, are essentially differences of degree. Motif Inferensi, Eksplanasi dan P ---  --- SUMBER 2: Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- General description of the scales --- The DASS is a set of three self-report scales designed to measure the negative emotional states of depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS was constructed not merely as another set of scales to measure conventionally defined emotional states, but to further the process of defining, understanding, and measuring the ubiquitous and clinically significant emotional states usually described as depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS should thus meet the requirements of both researchers and scientist-professional clinicians. --- Each of the three DASS scales contains 14 items, divided into subscales of 2-5 items with similar content.  The Depression scale assesses dysphoria, hopelessness, devaluation of life, self-deprecation, lack of interest/involvement, anhedonia, and inertia.  The Anxiety scale assesses autonomic arousal, skeletal muscle effects, situational anxiety, and subjective experience of anxious affect.  The Stress scale is sensitive to levels of chronic non-specific arousal.  It assesses difficulty relaxing, nervous arousal, and being easily upset/agitated, irritable/over-reactive and impatient.  Subjects are asked to use 4-point severity/frequency scales to rate the extent to which they have experienced each state --- over the past week --- .  Scores for Depression, Anxiety and Stress are calculated by summing the scores for the relevant items. --- In addition to the basic 42-item questionnaire, a short version, the DASS21, is available with 7 items per scale.  Note also that an earlier version of the DASS scales was referred to as the Self-Analysis Questionnaire (SAQ). --- As the scales of the DASS have been shown to have high internal consistency and to yield meaningful discriminations in a variety of settings, the scales should meet the needs of both researchers and clinicians who wish to measure current state or change in state over time (e.g., in the course of treatment) on the three dimensions of depression, anxiety and stress. --- Characteristics of high scorers on each DASS scale --- Depression scale --- self-disparaging --- dispirited, gloomy, blue --- convinced that life has no meaning or value --- pessimistic about the future --- unable to experience enjoyment or satisfaction --- unable to become interested or involved --- slow, lacking in initiative --- Anxiety scale --- apprehensive, panicky --- trembly, shaky --- aware of dryness of the mouth, breathing difficulties, pounding of the heart, sweatiness of the palms --- worried about performance and possible loss of control --- Stress scale --- over-aroused, tense --- unable to relax --- touchy, easily upset --- irritable --- easily startled --- nervy, jumpy, fidgety --- intolerant of interruption or delay --- The DASS in research --- The DASS may be administered either in groups or individually for research purposes.  The capacity to discriminate between the three related states of depression, anxiety and stress should be useful to researchers concerned with the nature, aetiology and mechanisms of emotional disturbance. --- As the essential development of the DASS was carried out with non-clinical samples, it is suitable for screening normal adolescents and adults.  Given the necessary language proficiency, there seems no compelling case against use of the scales for comparative purposes with children as young as 12 years.  It must be borne in mind, however, that the lower age limit of the development samples was 17 years. --- Clinical use of the DASS --- The principal value of the DASS in a clinical setting is to clarify the locus of emotional disturbance, as part of the broader task of clinical assessment.  The essential function of the DASS is to assess the severity of the --- core --- symptoms of depression, anxiety and stress.  It must be recognised that clinically depressed, anxious or stressed persons may well manifest additional symptoms that tend to be common to two or all three of the conditions, such as sleep, appetite, and sexual disturbances.  These disturbances will be elicited by clinical examination, or by the use of general symptom check lists as required. --- The DASS may be administered and scored by non-psychologists, but decisions based on particular score profiles should be made only by experienced clinicians who have carried out an appropriate clinical examination.  It should be noted also that none of the DASS items refers to suicidal tendencies because items relating to such tendencies were found not to load on any scale.  The experienced clinician will recognise the need to determine the risk of suicide in seriously disturbed persons. --- The DASS and diagnosis --- The DASS is based on a --- dimensional --- rather than a --- categorical --- conception of psychological disorder.  The assumption on which the DASS development was based (and which was confirmed by the research data) is that the differences between the depression, the anxiety, and the stress experienced by normal subjects and the clinically disturbed, are essentially differences of degree. Motif Inferensi, Eksplanasi dan P ---  --- SUMBER 2: Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- General description of the scales --- The DASS is a set of three self-report scales designed to measure the negative emotional states of depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS was constructed not merely as another set of scales to measure conventionally defined emotional states, but to further the process of defining, understanding, and measuring the ubiquitous and clinically significant emotional states usually described as depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS should thus meet the requirements of both researchers and scientist-professional clinicians. --- Each of the three DASS scales contains 14 items, divided into subscales of 2-5 items with similar content.  The Depression scale assesses dysphoria, hopelessness, devaluation of life, self-deprecation, lack of interest/involvement, anhedonia, and inertia. The Stress scale is sensitive to levels of chronic non-specific arousal.  It assesses difficulty relaxing, nervous arousal, and being easily upset/agitated, irritable/over-reactive and impatient.  Subjects are asked to use 4-point severity/frequency scales to rate the extent to which they have experienced each state --- over the past week --- .  Scores for Depression, Anxiety and Stress are calculated by summing the scores for the relevant items. --- In addition to the basic 42-item questionnaire, a short version, the DASS21, is available with 7 items per scale.  Note also that an earlier version of the DASS scales was referred to as the Self-Analysis Questionnaire (SAQ). --- As the scales of the DASS have been shown to have high internal consistency and to yield meaningful discriminations in a variety of settings, the scales should meet the needs of both researchers and clinicians who wish to measure current state or change in state over time (e.g., in the course of treatment) on the three dimensions of depression, anxiety and stress. --- Characteristics of high scorers on each DASS scale --- Depression scale --- self-disparaging --- dispirited, gloomy, blue --- convinced that life has no meaning or value --- pessimistic about the future --- unable to experience enjoyment or satisfaction --- unable to become interested or involved --- slow, lacking in initiative --- Anxiety scale --- apprehensive, panicky --- trembly, shaky --- aware of dryness of the mouth, breathing difficulties, pounding of the heart, sweatiness of the palms --- worried about performance and possible loss of control --- Stress scale --- over-aroused, tense --- unable to relax --- touchy, easily upset --- irritable --- easily startled --- nervy, jumpy, fidgety --- intolerant of interruption or delay --- The DASS in research --- The DASS may be administered either in groups or individually for research purposes.  The capacity to discriminate between the three related states of depression, anxiety and stress should be useful to researchers concerned with the nature, aetiology and mechanisms of emotional disturbance. --- As the essential development of the DASS was carried out with non-clinical samples, it is suitable for screening normal adolescents and adults.  Given the necessary language proficiency, there seems no compelling case against use of the scales for comparative purposes with children as young as 12 years.  It must be borne in mind, however, that the lower age limit of the development samples was 17 years. --- Clinical use of the DASS --- The principal value of the DASS in a clinical setting is to clarify the locus of emotional disturbance, as part of the broader task of clinical assessment.  The essential function of the DASS is to assess the severity of the --- core --- symptoms of depression, anxiety and stress.  It must be recognised that clinically depressed, anxious or stressed persons may well manifest additional symptoms that tend to be common to two or all three of the conditions, such as sleep, appetite, and sexual disturbances.  These disturbances will be elicited by clinical examination, or by the use of general symptom check lists as required. --- The DASS may be administered and scored by non-psychologists, but decisions based on particular score profiles should be made only by experienced clinicians who have carried out an appropriate clinical examination.  It should be noted also that none of the DASS items refers to suicidal tendencies because items relating to such tendencies were found not to load on any scale.  The experienced clinician will recognise the need to determine the risk of suicide in seriously disturbed persons. --- The DASS and diagnosis --- The DASS is based on a --- dimensional --- rather than a --- categorical --- conception of psychological disorder.  The assumption on which the DASS development was based (and which was confirmed by the research data) is that the differences between the depression, the anxiety, and the stress experienced by normal subjects and the clinically disturbed, are essentially differences of degree. Motif Inferensi, Eksplanasi dan P ---  --- SUMBER 2: Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- General description of the scales --- The DASS is a set of three self-report scales designed to measure the negative emotional states of depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS was constructed not merely as another set of scales to measure conventionally defined emotional states, but to further the process of defining, understanding, and measuring the ubiquitous and clinically significant emotional states usually described as depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS should thus meet the requirements of both researchers and scientist-professional clinicians. --- Each of the three DASS scales contains 14 items, divided into subscales of 2-5 items with similar content.  The Depression scale assesses dysphoria, hopelessness, devaluation of life, self-deprecation, lack of interest/involvement, anhedonia, and inertia.  The Anxiety scale assesses autonomic arousal, skeletal muscle effects, situational anxiety, and subjective experience of anxious affect.  The Stress scale is sensitive to levels of chronic non-specific arousal.  It assesses difficulty relaxing, nervous arousal, and being easily upset/agitated, irritable/over-reactive and impatient.  Subjects are asked to use 4-point severity/frequency scales to rate the extent to which they have experienced each state --- over the past week --- .  Scores for Depression, Anxiety and Stress are calculated by summing the scores for the relevant items. --- In addition to the basic 42-item questionnaire, a short version, the DASS21, is available with 7 items per scale.  Note also that an earlier version of the DASS scales was referred to as the Self-Analysis Questionnaire (SAQ). --- As the scales of the DASS have been shown to have high internal consistency and to yield meaningful discriminations in a variety of settings, the scales should meet the needs of both researchers and clinicians who wish to measure current state or change in state over time (e.g., in the course of treatment) on the three dimensions of depression, anxiety and stress. --- Characteristics of high scorers on each DASS scale --- Depression scale --- self-disparaging --- dispirited, gloomy, blue --- convinced that life has no meaning or value --- pessimistic about the future --- unable to experience enjoyment or satisfaction --- unable to become interested or involved --- slow, lacking in initiative --- Anxiety scale --- apprehensive, panicky --- trembly, shaky --- aware of dryness of the mouth, breathing difficulties, pounding of the heart, sweatiness of the palms --- worried about performance and possible loss of control --- Stress scale --- over-aroused, tense --- unable to relax --- touchy, easily upset --- irritable --- easily startled --- nervy, jumpy, fidgety --- intolerant of interruption or delay --- The DASS in research --- The DASS may be administered either in groups or individually for research purposes.  The capacity to discriminate between the three related states of depression, anxiety and stress should be useful to researchers concerned with the nature, aetiology and mechanisms of emotional disturbance. --- As the essential development of the DASS was carried out with non-clinical samples, it is suitable for screening normal adolescents and adults.  Given the necessary language proficiency, there seems no compelling case against use of the scales for comparative purposes with children as young as 12 years.  It must be borne in mind, however, that the lower age limit of the development samples was 17 years. --- Clinical use of the DASS --- The principal value of the DASS in a clinical setting is to clarify the locus of emotional disturbance, as part of the broader task of clinical assessment.  The essential function of the DASS is to assess the severity of the --- core --- symptoms of depression, anxiety and stress.  It must be recognised that clinically depressed, anxious or stressed persons may well manifest additional symptoms that tend to be common to two or all three of the conditions, such as sleep, appetite, and sexual disturbances.  These disturbances will be elicited by clinical examination, or by the use of general symptom check lists as required. --- The DASS may be administered and scored by non-psychologists, but decisions based on particular score profiles should be made only by experienced clinicians who have carried out an appropriate clinical examination.  It should be noted also that none of the DASS items refers to suicidal tendencies because items relating to such tendencies were found not to load on any scale.  The experienced clinician will recognise the need to determine the risk of suicide in seriously disturbed persons. --- The DASS and diagnosis --- The DASS is based on a --- dimensional --- rather than a --- categorical --- conception of psychological disorder.  The assumption on which the DASS development was based (and which was confirmed by the research data) is that the differences between the depression, the anxiety, and the stress experienced by normal subjects and the clinically disturbed, are essentially differences of degree.  The DASS therefo ---  ---             PERTANYAAN / KONTEKS USER: ---             Hallo ChatGPT, nama saya Fawwaz Muhammad Arifin. dan saya saat ini berada di 8G. e-mail saya di fawwazmuhammadarifin99@gmail.com . saya sudah mengisi kuisioner DASS21 dengan detail pertanyaan dan jawaban :- Saya merasa sulit untuk beristirahat dan saya menjawab 1 - Motif Inferensi, Eksplanasi dan P ---  --- SUMBER 2: Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- General description of the scales --- The DASS is a set of three self-report scales designed to measure the negative emotional states of depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS was constructed not merely as another set of scales to measure conventionally defined emotional states, but to further the process of defining, understanding, and measuring the ubiquitous and clinically significant emotional states usually described as depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS should thus meet the requirements of both researchers and scientist-professional clinicians. --- Each of the three DASS scales contains 14 items, divided into subscales of 2-5 items with similar content.  The Depression scale assesses dysphoria, hopelessness, devaluation of life, self-deprecation, lack of interest/involvement, anhedonia, and inertia.  The Anxiety scale assesses autonomic arousal, skeletal muscle effects, situational anxiety, and subjective experience of anxious affect.  The Stress scale is sensitive to levels of chronic non-specific arousal.  It assesses difficulty relaxing, nervous arousal, and being easily upset/agitated, irritable/over-reactive and impatient.  Subjects are asked to use 4-point severity/frequency scales to rate the extent to which they have experienced each state --- over the past week --- .  Scores for Depression, Anxiety and Stress are calculated by summing the scores for the relevant items. --- In addition to the basic 42-item questionnaire, a short version, the DASS21, is available with 7 items per scale.  Note also that an earlier version of the DASS scales was referred to as the Self-Analysis Questionnaire (SAQ). --- As the scales of the DASS have been shown to have high internal consistency and to yield meaningful discriminations in a variety of settings, the scales should meet the needs of both researchers and clinicians who wish to measure current state or change in state over time (e.g., in the course of treatment) on the three dimensions of depression, anxiety and stress. --- Characteristics of high scorers on each DASS scale --- Depression scale --- self-disparaging --- dispirited, gloomy, blue --- convinced that life has no meaning or value --- pessimistic about the future --- unable to experience enjoyment or satisfaction --- unable to become interested or involved --- slow, lacking in initiative --- Anxiety scale --- apprehensive, panicky --- trembly, shaky --- aware of dryness of the mouth, breathing difficulties, pounding of the heart, sweatiness of the palms --- worried about performance and possible loss of control --- Stress scale --- over-aroused, tense --- unable to relax --- touchy, easily upset --- irritable --- easily startled --- nervy, jumpy, fidgety --- intolerant of interruption or delay --- The DASS in research --- The DASS may be administered either in groups or individually for research purposes.  The capacity to discriminate between the three related states of depression, anxiety and stress should be useful to researchers concerned with the nature, aetiology and mechanisms of emotional disturbance. --- As the essential development of the DASS was carried out with non-clinical samples, it is suitable for screening normal adolescents and adults.  Given the necessary language proficiency, there seems no compelling case against use of the scales for comparative purposes with children as young as 12 years.  It must be borne in mind, however, that the lower age limit of the development samples was 17 years. --- Clinical use of the DASS --- The principal value of the DASS in a clinical setting is to clarify the locus of emotional disturbance, as part of the broader task of clinical assessment.  The essential function of the DASS is to assess the severity of the --- core --- symptoms of depression, anxiety and stress.  It must be recognised that clinically depressed, anxious or stressed persons may well manifest additional symptoms that tend to be common to two or all three of the conditions, such as sleep, appetite, and sexual disturbances.  These disturbances will be elicited by clinical examination, or by the use of general symptom check lists as required. --- The DASS may be administered and scored by non-psychologists, but decisions based on particular score profiles should be made only by experienced clinicians who have carried out an appropriate clinical examination.  It should be noted also that none of the DASS items refers to suicidal tendencies because items relating to such tendencies were found not to load on any scale.  The experienced clinician will recognise the need to determine the risk of suicide in seriously disturbed persons. --- The DASS and diagnosis --- The DASS is based on a --- dimensional --- rather than a --- categorical --- conception of psychological disorder.  The assumption on which the DASS development was based (and which was confirmed by the research data) is that the differences between the depression, the anxiety, and the stress experienced by normal subjects and the clinically disturbed, are essentially differences of degree. Motif Inferensi, Eksplanasi dan P ---  --- SUMBER 2: Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- General description of the scales --- The DASS is a set of three self-report scales designed to measure the negative emotional states of depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS was constructed not merely as another set of scales to measure conventionally defined emotional states, but to further the process of defining, understanding, and measuring the ubiquitous and clinically significant emotional states usually described as depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS should thus meet the requirements of both researchers and scientist-professional clinicians. --- Each of the three DASS scales contains 14 items, divided into subscales of 2-5 items with similar content.  The Depression scale assesses dysphoria, hopelessness, devaluation of life, self-deprecation, lack of interest/involvement, anhedonia, and inertia.  The Anxiety scale assesses autonomic arousal, skeletal muscle effects, situational anxiety, and subjective experience of anxious affect.  The Stress scale is sensitive to levels of chronic non-specific arousal.  It assesses difficulty relaxing, nervous arousal, and being easily upset/agitated, irritable/over-reactive and impatient.  Subjects are asked to use 4-point severity/frequency scales to rate the extent to which they have experienced each state --- over the past week --- .  Scores for Depression, Anxiety and Stress are calculated by summing the scores for the relevant items. --- In addition to the basic 42-item questionnaire, a short version, the DASS21, is available with 7 items per scale.  Note also that an earlier version of the DASS scales was referred to as the Self-Analysis Questionnaire (SAQ). --- As the scales of the DASS have been shown to have high internal consistency and to yield meaningful discriminations in a variety of settings, the scales should meet the needs of both researchers and clinicians who wish to measure current state or change in state over time (e.g., in the course of treatment) on the three dimensions of depression, anxiety and stress. --- Characteristics of high scorers on each DASS scale --- Depression scale --- self-disparaging --- dispirited, gloomy, blue --- convinced that life has no meaning or value --- pessimistic about the future --- unable to experience enjoyment or satisfaction --- unable to become interested or involved --- slow, lacking in initiative --- Anxiety scale --- apprehensive, panicky --- trembly, shaky --- aware of dryness of the mouth, breathing difficulties, pounding of the heart, sweatiness of the palms --- worried about performance and possible loss of control --- Stress scale --- over-aroused, tense --- unable to relax --- touchy, easily upset --- irritable --- easily startled --- nervy, jumpy, fidgety --- intolerant of interruption or delay --- The DASS in research --- The DASS may be administered either in groups or individually for research purposes.  The capacity to discriminate between the three related states of depression, anxiety and stress should be useful to researchers concerned with the nature, aetiology and mechanisms of emotional disturbance. --- As the essential development of the DASS was carried out with non-clinical samples, it is suitable for screening normal adolescents and adults.  Given the necessary language proficiency, there seems no compelling case against use of the scales for comparative purposes with children as young as 12 years.  It must be borne in mind, however, that the lower age limit of the development samples was 17 years. --- Clinical use of the DASS --- The principal value of the DASS in a clinical setting is to clarify the locus of emotional disturbance, as part of the broader task of clinical assessment.  The essential function of the DASS is to assess the severity of the --- core --- symptoms of depression, anxiety and stress.  It must be recognised that clinically depressed, anxious or stressed persons may well manifest additional symptoms that tend to be common to two or all three of the conditions, such as sleep, appetite, and sexual disturbances.  These disturbances will be elicited by clinical examination, or by the use of general symptom check lists as required. --- The DASS may be administered and scored by non-psychologists, but decisions based on particular score profiles should be made only by experienced clinicians who have carried out an appropriate clinical examination.  It should be noted also that none of the DASS items refers to suicidal tendencies because items relating to such tendencies were found not to load on any scale.  The experienced clinician will recognise the need to determine the risk of suicide in seriously disturbed persons. --- The DASS and diagnosis --- The DASS is based on a --- dimensional --- rather than a --- categorical --- conception of psychological disorder.  The assumption on which the DASS development was based (and which was confirmed by the research data) is that the differences between the depression, the anxiety, and the stress experienced by normal subjects and the clinically disturbed, are essentially differences of degree. 16-Jun-2026-11:34:01|ID7EB360|USERRESPONSE[7]="cemas karena gatau mamu masukin materi apa"
16-Jun-2026-11:34:02|ID7EB360|CHATGPT[8]="Ya, itu gambaran yang jelas. Jadi yang dominan bukan cuma “takut nilai”, tapi cemas yang muncul karena kamu merasa tidak ada pegangan: kamu bingung menentukan materi apa yang harus masuk, kriteria “cukup” itu tidak terasa jelas. Dari sini biasanya otak akan terus mencari kepastian, tapi karena kepastiannya tidak langsung muncul, kamu jadi tegang, sulit bersantai, dan akhirnya muncul perasaan kurang inisiatif atau sedih karena terasa tidak efektif.   ---  --- Biar aku bisa memahami pemicunya: acuan materi yang harus dimasukkan biasanya kamu dapat dari apa—panduan dosen, rumusan masalah di RPS, atau cuma dari kemampuan menafsir sendiri?"

Motif Inferensi, Eksplanasi dan P ---  --- SUMBER 2: Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- General description of the scales --- The DASS is a set of three self-report scales designed to measure the negative emotional states of depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS was constructed not merely as another set of scales to measure conventionally defined emotional states, but to further the process of defining, understanding, and measuring the ubiquitous and clinically significant emotional states usually described as depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS should thus meet the requirements of both researchers and scientist-professional clinicians. --- Each of the three DASS scales contains 14 items, divided into subscales of 2-5 items with similar content.  The Depression scale assesses dysphoria, hopelessness, devaluation of life, self-deprecation, lack of interest/involvement, anhedonia, and inertia.  The Anxiety scale assesses autonomic arousal, skeletal muscle effects, situational anxiety, and subjective experience of anxious affect.  The Stress scale is sensitive to levels of chronic non-specific arousal.  It assesses difficulty relaxing, nervous arousal, and being easily upset/agitated, irritable/over-reactive and impatient.  Subjects are asked to use 4-point severity/frequency scales to rate the extent to which they have experienced each state --- over the past week --- .  Scores for Depression, Anxiety and Stress are calculated by summing the scores for the relevant items. --- In addition to the basic 42-item questionnaire, a short version, the DASS21, is available with 7 items per scale.  Note also that an earlier version of the DASS scales was referred to as the Self-Analysis Questionnaire (SAQ). --- As the scales of the DASS have been shown to have high internal consistency and to yield meaningful discriminations in a variety of settings, the scales should meet the needs of both researchers and clinicians who wish to measure current state or change in state over time (e.g., in the course of treatment) on the three dimensions of depression, anxiety and stress. --- Characteristics of high scorers on each DASS scale --- Depression scale --- self-disparaging --- dispirited, gloomy, blue --- convinced that life has no meaning or value --- pessimistic about the future --- unable to experience enjoyment or satisfaction --- unable to become interested or involved --- slow, lacking in initiative --- Anxiety scale --- apprehensive, panicky --- trembly, shaky --- aware of dryness of the mouth, breathing difficulties, pounding of the heart, sweatiness of the palms --- worried about performance and possible loss of control --- Stress scale --- over-aroused, tense --- unable to relax --- touchy, easily upset --- irritable --- easily startled --- nervy, jumpy, fidgety --- intolerant of interruption or delay --- The DASS in research --- The DASS may be administered either in groups or individually for research purposes.  The capacity to discriminate between the three related states of depression, anxiety and stress should be useful to researchers concerned with the nature, aetiology and mechanisms of emotional disturbance. --- As the essential development of the DASS was carried out with non-clinical samples, it is suitable for screening normal adolescents and adults.  Given the necessary language proficiency, there seems no compelling case against use of the scales for comparative purposes with children as young as 12 years.  It must be borne in mind, however, that the lower age limit of the development samples was 17 years. --- Clinical use of the DASS --- The principal value of the DASS in a clinical setting is to clarify the locus of emotional disturbance, as part of the broader task of clinical assessment.  The essential function of the DASS is to assess the severity of the --- core --- symptoms of depression, anxiety and stress.  It must be recognised that clinically depressed, anxious or stressed persons may well manifest additional symptoms that tend to be common to two or all three of the conditions, such as sleep, appetite, and sexual disturbances.  These disturbances will be elicited by clinical examination, or by the use of general symptom check lists as required. --- The DASS may be administered and scored by non-psychologists, but decisions based on particular score profiles should be made only by experienced clinicians who have carried out an appropriate clinical examination.  It should be noted also that none of the DASS items refers to suicidal tendencies because items relating to such tendencies were found not to load on any scale.  The experienced clinician will recognise the need to determine the risk of suicide in seriously disturbed persons. --- The DASS and diagnosis --- The DASS is based on a --- dimensional --- rather than a --- categorical --- conception of psychological disorder.  The assumption on which the DASS development was based (and which was confirmed by the research data) is that the differences between the depression, the anxiety, and the stress experienced by normal subjects and the clinically disturbed, are essentially differences of degree.  The DASS therefo ---  ---             PERTANYAAN / KONTEKS USER: ---             Hallo ChatGPT, nama saya Fauzul Arifin. dan saya saat ini berada di 12. e-mail saya di fauzularifin99@gmail.com . saya sudah mengisi kuisioner DASS21 dengan detail pertanyaan dan jawaban :- Saya merasa sulit untuk beristirahat dan saya menjawab 1 - Saya merasa bibir saya sering kering dan saya menjawab 1 - Saya sama sekali tidak dapat merasakan perasaan positif dan saya menjawab 3 - Saya mengalami kesulitan bernafas (misalnya: sesak atau tidak dapat bernafas padahal tidak melakukan aktivitas fisik sebelumnya) dan saya menjawab 2 - Saya merasa sulit untuk mengembangkan inisiatif untuk melakukan sesuatu. dan saya menjawab 1 - Saya cenderung bereaksi berlebihan terhadap suatu situasi. dan saya menjawab 3 - Saya mengalami gemetar (misalnya di tangan). dan saya menjawab 2 - Saya merasa sulit untuk bersantai. dan saya menjawab 1 - Saya khawatir tentang situasi di mana saya mungkin panik dan membuat bodoh diriku sendiri dan saya menjawab 0 - Saya merasa tidak ada hal yang dapat diharapkan di masa depan. dan saya menjawab 2 - Saya merasa gelisah. dan saya menjawab 0 - Saya merasa sulit untuk bersantai. dan saya menjawab 0 - Saya merasa sedih dan tertekan. dan saya menjawab 2 - Saya menemukan diri saya menjadi tidak sabar ketika mengalami penundaan (misalnya: kemacetan lalu lintas, menunggu sesuatu). dan saya menjawab 3 - Saya merasa lemas seperti mau pingsan. dan saya menjawab 0 - Saya merasa saya kehilangan minat akan segala hal. dan saya menjawab 2 - Saya merasa bahwa saya tidak berharga sebagai seorang manusia. dan saya menjawab 2 - Saya merasa bahwa saya mudah tersinggung. dan saya menjawab 0 - Saya berkeringat secara berlebihan (misalnya: tangan berkeringat), padahal temperatur tidak panas atau tidak melakukan aktivitas fisik sebelumnya. dan saya menjawab 1 - Saya merasa takut tanpa alasan yang jelas. dan saya menjawab 1- Saya merasa bahwa hidup tidak ada artinya. dan saya menjawab 1. Untuk anamnesis yang lebih tepat, aku ingin memahami kondisi kamu sekarang: dalam 1 minggu terakhir, gejala yang paling mengganggu kamu adalah yang mana, depresi, kecemasan, atau stres, dan bisa ceritakan contoh kejadian nyatanya?"

16-Jun-2026-12:33:03|IDA3BF00|CHATGPT[2]="Oke, Fauzul—kalau kamu bilang sekarang kamu cemas, itu penting banget kita fokuskan ke pengalaman kamu saat ini. Dari skor kamu, kecemasan (anxiety) memang berada di level yang cukup berarti, jadi aku ingin tahu detailnya: saat cemas itu muncul, pikiran utamanya lebih ke kekhawatiran akan “panik/kehilangan kontrol” seperti yang kamu pilih, atau lebih ke hal lain (misalnya masalah di sekolah/kerja, kesehatan, hubungan, atau masa depan)?"
16-Jun-2026-12:33:23|IDA3BF00|USERRESPONSE[2]="lebih ke khawatir aja --- "
16-Jun-2026-12:33:24|IDA3BF00|CHATGPT[3]="Paham, jadi kecemasannya lebih dominan berupa kekhawatiran—bukan panik yang benar-benar terjadi, tapi lebih seperti pikiran terus memutar tentang kemungkinan buruk. Supaya aku bisa menangkap pola kekhawatiran kamu, biasanya kekhawatiran itu paling sering muncul saat situasi seperti apa (misalnya sendirian, menjelang tidur, di keramaian/di tempat tertentu, tugas atau deadline, atau setelah kejadian tertentu)?"
16-Jun-2026-12:33:37|IDA3BF00|USERRESPONSE[3]="kalau ada tugas menumpuk --- "
16-Jun-2026-12:33:39|IDA3BF00|CHATGPT[4]="Masuk banget—tugas menumpuk memang sering jadi pemicu utama: otak seperti “menjaga” agar kamu tidak salah langkah, tapi akhirnya berubah jadi kekhawatiran yang terus jalan dan bikin tubuh ikut tegang. Dari pengalamanmu saat tugas menumpuk, biasanya yang paling mengganggu itu bagian mana: kamu jadi sulit mulai (inisiasi rendah), jadi sulit santai/terus gelisah, atau lebih sering merasa pikiranmu menilai kamu “tidak berharga” atau “gagal”?"

Motif Inferensi, Eksplanasi dan P ---  --- SUMBER 2: Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- Overview of the DASS and its uses --- General description of the scales --- The DASS is a set of three self-report scales designed to measure the negative emotional states of depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS was constructed not merely as another set of scales to measure conventionally defined emotional states, but to further the process of defining, understanding, and measuring the ubiquitous and clinically significant emotional states usually described as depression, anxiety and stress.  The DASS should thus meet the requirements of both researchers and scientist-professional clinicians. --- Each of the three DASS scales contains 14 items, divided into subscales of 2-5 items with similar content.  The Depression scale assesses dysphoria, hopelessness, devaluation of life, self-deprecation, lack of interest/involvement, anhedonia, and inertia.  The Anxiety scale assesses autonomic arousal, skeletal muscle effects, situational anxiety, and subjective experience of anxious affect.  The Stress scale is sensitive to levels of chronic non-specific arousal.  It assesses difficulty relaxing, nervous arousal, and being easily upset/agitated, irritable/over-reactive and impatient.  Subjects are asked to use 4-point severity/frequency scales to rate the extent to which they have experienced each state --- over the past week --- .  Scores for Depression, Anxiety and Stress are calculated by summing the scores for the relevant items. --- In addition to the basic 42-item questionnaire, a short version, the DASS21, is available with 7 items per scale.  Note also that an earlier version of the DASS scales was referred to as the Self-Analysis Questionnaire (SAQ). --- As the scales of the DASS have been shown to have high internal consistency and to yield meaningful discriminations in a variety of settings, the scales should meet the needs of both researchers and clinicians who wish to measure current state or change in state over time (e.g., in the course of treatment) on the three dimensions of depression, anxiety and stress. --- Characteristics of high scorers on each DASS scale --- Depression scale --- self-disparaging --- dispirited, gloomy, blue --- convinced that life has no meaning or value --- pessimistic about the future --- unable to experience enjoyment or satisfaction --- unable to become interested or involved --- slow, lacking in initiative --- Anxiety scale --- apprehensive, panicky --- trembly, shaky --- aware of dryness of the mouth, breathing difficulties, pounding of the heart, sweatiness of the palms --- worried about performance and possible loss of control --- Stress scale --- over-aroused, tense --- unable to relax --- touchy, easily upset --- irritable --- easily startled --- nervy, jumpy, fidgety --- intolerant of interruption or delay --- The DASS in research --- The DASS may be administered either in groups or individually for research purposes.  The capacity to discriminate between the three related states of depression, anxiety and stress should be useful to researchers concerned with the nature, aetiology and mechanisms of emotional disturbance. --- As the essential development of the DASS was carried out with non-clinical samples, it is suitable for screening normal adolescents and adults.  Given the necessary language proficiency, there seems no compelling case against use of the scales for comparative purposes with children as young as 12 years.  It must be borne in mind, however, that the lower age limit of the development samples was 17 years. --- Clinical use of the DASS --- The principal value of the DASS in a clinical setting is to clarify the locus of emotional disturbance, as part of the broader task of clinical assessment.  The essential function of the DASS is to assess the severity of the --- core --- symptoms of depression, anxiety and stress.  It must be recognised that clinically depressed, anxious or stressed persons may well manifest additional symptoms that tend to be common to two or all three of the conditions, such as sleep, appetite, and sexual disturbances.  These disturbances will be elicited by clinical examination, or by the use of general symptom check lists as required. --- The DASS may be administered and scored by non-psychologists, but decisions based on particular score profiles should be made only by experienced clinicians who have carried out an appropriate clinical examination.  It should be noted also that none of the DASS items refers to suicidal tendencies because items relating to such tendencies were found not to load on any scale.  The experienced clinician will recognise the need to determine the risk of suicide in seriously disturbed persons. --- The DASS and diagnosis --- The DASS is based on a --- dimensional --- rather than a --- categorical --- conception of psychological disorder.  The assumption on which the DASS development was based (and which was confirmed by the research data) is that the differences between the depression, the anxiety, and the stress experienced by normal subjects and the clinically disturbed, are essentially differences of degree.
